## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed lists a canonical routing map, a supporting research brief, and four public ecosystem pointers, but it does not assign claim-level authority, retrieval state, or invalidation conditions to those different source types
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because navigation policy, research provenance, local convention, and current framework behavior have different change rates and cannot safely share one undifferentiated authority label
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the research brief's links are treated as freshly reviewed, the map's jump points are treated as implementation rules, Spring evidence drives Ktor work, or one generic Kotlin source overrides local build behavior
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: do not mark links current without retrieval, do not let a routing source replace the destination's content, and keep observed repository evidence separate from archived policy
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain all six rows while adding source operation, claim scope, freshness, framework match, local proof, and invalidation metadata
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the source map should route not only by topic but by evidence operation: navigate, establish provenance, inspect local convention, refresh external semantics, or escalate ownership

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed records context-free summaries, unsourced claims, and unverified instructions, but source routing also fails through overloading, keyword matches, circular authority, stale paths, and ownership leakage
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a wrong route can produce polished, well-cited guidance that never reaches the source owning the actual reliability boundary
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the registry becomes a preference against broad reading, rejects legitimate multi-boundary tasks, forbids secondary sources entirely, or flags a stale path without checking whether an equivalent destination exists
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply smell detection to the route and claim under review, allowing justified multi-source plans with explicit subdecision ownership
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to keep the three seed rows and add routing-specific signals, exceptions, correction paths, and misroute tests

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed provides Adopt, Adapt, Avoid, and Cost of being wrong rows centered on evidence agreement, but it does not compare route precision, context cost, freshness work, destination ownership, and reversibility
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because routing trades search time and context volume against the much larger cost of implementing advice from the wrong authority
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: Adopt means blind map compliance, Adapt quietly changes ownership, Avoid ends without a route, or high-cost language is used to justify unlimited research
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: evaluate viable sources within the target repository and technology, and keep escalation proportional to real downstream harm

- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the deeper deduction is that source count is a weak capacity proxy; independent authority conflicts and context bytes are better predictors of routing difficulty

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed identifies source drift, generic advice, implicit decisions, and list-like large corpora, but it does not specify how to detect, reproduce, or recover from each routing failure
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a failure label is operational only when a reviewer can distinguish a bad map, stale source, ambiguous classifier, destination gap, or unranked corpus
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: source drift is inferred from age alone, generic advice is detected only by wording, implicit decisions gain a table but no owner, or a large corpus is merely split into smaller unranked lists
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: test failure scenarios in local or synthetic contexts and do not mutate canonical source roles without owner evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain each seed row while adding fault injection, route trace, discrimination, recovery proof, owner, and invalidation controls
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that routing failures are often failures of classification or ownership before they are failures of retrieval; adding search capacity cannot repair an undefined destination

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where source drift is inferred from age alone, generic advice is detected only by wording, implicit decisions gain a table but no owner, or a large corpus is merely split into smaller unranked lists
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within test failure scenarios in local or synthetic contexts and do not mutate canonical source roles without owner evidence
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: retain each seed row while adding fault injection, route trace, discrimination, recovery proof, owner, and invalidation controls
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: repair a path, update a classifier, add destination ownership, collapse duplicates, introduce ranked canonical roles, route to a specialist, or preserve a conflict for owner resolution This changes how the section resolves which routing failures must be modeled explicitly and what evidence shows that mitigation restores a correct next-source decision.

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed requires classified bounded retries, one stale-evidence refresh, backpressure, checkpoints, and exclusive ownership, but it does not distinguish a source retry from an uncontrolled research or routing loop
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because unclassified retries erase why the route failed and can accumulate context until the original decision disappears
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: agents search repeatedly until finding agreeable guidance, source refresh silently changes the question, broken destinations trigger broad browsing, or work continues while heading, uniqueness, or ownership gates are red
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: never retry to achieve a preferred answer, never discard the first failure, and keep one writer per routing artifact
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend the inherited workflow with a routing-failure taxonomy, controlled source retries, context budgets, first-route preservation, and loop detection
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure protects decision identity: stopping context growth preserves the question and evidence chain needed to decide whether re-routing is justified
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify failure as transient access, stale path, missing destination, ambiguous boundary, conflicting authority, duplicate source, or wrong route; retry only a named hypothesis once unless policy states otherwise, retaining the first route and source state
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because unclassified retries erase why the route failed and can accumulate context until the original decision disappears
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; agents search repeatedly until finding agreeable guidance, source refresh silently changes the question, broken destinations trigger broad browsing, or work continues while heading, uniqueness, or ownership gates are red
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: never retry to achieve a preferred answer, never discard the first failure, and keep one writer per routing artifact
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: extend the inherited workflow with a routing-failure taxonomy, controlled source retries, context budgets, first-route preservation, and loop detection

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed records loaded sources, proof, timing, reviewer decision, uncertainty, refresh trigger, and compact evidence, but it does not expose the route transitions needed to diagnose a wrong destination
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a final link cannot show whether the classifier, map, path, hierarchy, freshness check, or destination content caused success or failure
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: raw tool output replaces decisions, source and route errors share one label, retries overwrite the first route, context size is unmeasured, or public retrieval metadata is omitted
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: capture the minimum reproducible trace, never secrets or private content, and avoid high-cardinality monitoring labels for raw questions
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to split inherited observations into classifier, candidate, source-state, context, destination, gate, correction, privacy, and handoff signals
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that routing observability is most valuable at decision boundaries: knowing why a source was rejected often saves more future context than recording every source that was opened

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed stops this reference at multiple systems, ownership boundaries, unbounded discovery, or production traffic without an SLO, but it does not explain how to federate source maps and preserve cross-boundary evidence
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a global map without local owners becomes stale, while isolated maps without contracts create duplicate and conflicting routes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: parallel agents edit one hierarchy, each repository invents incompatible labels, a central list has no destination owners, or splitting leaves generic-to-backend handoffs untested
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: do not use this single reference as a global source registry for independent systems and preserve one verification owner per split plus a named integration owner
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add federation criteria, map ownership, shared-schema limits, cross-map handoffs, privacy, refresh, and merge verification
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that source routing architecture mirrors organizational ownership; stale maps frequently reveal missing maintainers or unclear decision boundaries before they reveal search defects

## Section 026: Evidence Boundary Notes
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed defines local facts, external facts, and combined inference, but routing work also needs to distinguish navigation rules, supporting provenance, unrefreshed pointers, repository observations, executable results, and unresolved conflicts
- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because source routes blend where-to-look policy with substantive evidence, and collapsing them lets a map bullet or URL masquerade as implementation proof
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a URL becomes an external fact without retrieval, a map heading is quoted as destination guidance, repository behavior is generalized, inference is written as canonical policy, or conflict disappears in synthesis
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: do not upgrade confidence through repetition, preserve conflicts until discriminating evidence exists, and scope executable results to observed versions and environments
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend the three retained labels with navigation, provenance, retrieval state, repository observation, executable result, conflict, confidence, and invalidation metadata

- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from source routes blend where-to-look policy with substantive evidence, and collapsing them lets a map bullet or URL masquerade as implementation proof
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where a URL becomes an external fact without retrieval, a map heading is quoted as destination guidance, repository behavior is generalized, inference is written as canonical policy, or conflict disappears in synthesis
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within do not upgrade confidence through repetition, preserve conflicts until discriminating evidence exists, and scope executable results to observed versions and environments
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: extend the three retained labels with navigation, provenance, retrieval state, repository observation, executable result, conflict, confidence, and invalidation metadata
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: downgrade to provisional routing, present competing destinations, run a discriminating local check, request current primary evidence, or assign an owner without forcing consensus This changes how the section resolves how every source route should expose what is known, what was merely pointed to, what was observed locally, and what remains an inference.
